This flowchart is the National Law Relationship Test. Print it. Put it on your desk. Use it every time you start a research task. Appendix B provides a detachable version.

3.4 Conflict Resolution Rules

When provisions from different tiers conflict, apply these eight rules in order:

Rule 1: The Constitution prevails over all other sources, including the BOL itself. No provision of the BOL, no BAA, and no executive issuance can contradict the Constitution. If a BAA violates a constitutional provision, it is void — regardless of whether the subject is within the 55 enumerated powers.11

Rule 2: The BOL prevails over all BAAs. If a BAA contradicts a provision of the BOL, the BOL controls. BAAs are enacted under the BOL’s grant of authority. They cannot exceed that grant.

Rule 3: For national laws vs. BAAs — apply the National Law Relationship Test. This is the rule that both existing guidebooks acknowledge but neither reduces to a simple formula. Use the three-step test from Section 3.3. The answer depends on the subject.

Rule 4: BAA 13 organizes government; specific BAAs prevail on their subject matter. BAA 13 (the Administrative Code) provides the general organizational framework. When a specific BAA addresses the same subject in greater detail, the specific BAA prevails on its subject matter (lex specialis). Example: BAA 13 assigns the general mandate of MBHTE, but BAA 18 (the Education Code) defines the educational system in detail. For education matters, BAA 18 controls.

Rule 5: Later BAAs prevail over earlier BAAs on the same subject (lex posterior). When two BAAs conflict on the same subject, the more recently enacted BAA prevails — unless the earlier BAA contains a provision that the later BAA does not expressly repeal.

Rule 6: Specific BAAs prevail over general BAAs on overlapping topics (lex specialis). When a general BAA (like BAA 13) and a specific BAA (like BAA 84 on the budget system) overlap, the specific BAA governs on its subject matter.

Rule 7: Executive issuances cannot exceed the authority of the BAA they implement. An executive order, administrative order, or memorandum circular cannot contradict the BAA it implements. It also cannot expand the BAA’s scope beyond Parliament’s intent. If an IRR adds requirements not found in the BAA, those additional requirements may be challenged as ultra vires.

Rule 8: Jurisprudence provides binding interpretation of all other sources. Supreme Court decisions define the boundaries of BARMM authority. When the SC rules on the validity of a BAA, the scope of BOL provisions, or the limits of regional autonomy, that ruling is binding on all government bodies. The SC’s interpretation becomes part of the legal landscape — your research must account for it.12

3.5 Shari’ah Checkpoint: The Parallel Dimension

Before completing any hierarchy analysis, ask: Does this research question have a Shari’ah dimension?

Shari’ah is not a separate tier. It is a parallel legal dimension that intersects all seven tiers. The Constitution enables it (Art. X, Sec. 20, which empowers the organic act to create a Shari’ah-based justice system). The BOL codifies it (Art. X, Secs. 1-20). BAAs may implement it. National law (PD 1083) predates the BOL’s Shari’ah provisions. Jurisprudence interprets its boundaries.

A Shari’ah dimension exists when the subject involves: - Personal law for Muslims (marriage, divorce, inheritance, custody) - Property relations between Muslims - Commercial or civil actions between Muslims not covered by PD 1083 - Minor criminal offenses under Shari’ah court jurisdiction (ta’zir) - Islamic finance, halal regulation, waqf (endowment), or zakat (alms)

If a Shari’ah dimension exists, add a Shari’ah column to your Comparative Matrix and proceed to Chapter 9 for the full research methodology. The National Law Relationship Test still applies — you still need to determine which tier controls — but you also need to determine how Shari’ah interacts with the secular legal framework at each tier.

Chapter 9 covers this in detail. For now, the checkpoint ensures you do not complete your hierarchy analysis without asking the question.

3.6 Worked Example

Research question: What law governs public procurement in BARMM?

Step 1: National Law Relationship Test

Is procurement within the 55 enumerated powers? Art. V, Sec. 2 does not list “procurement” as a named power, but several enumerated powers necessarily involve procurement: (b) Administrative organization, (f) Budgeting, (qq) Public works and infrastructure, (bb) Health, etc. The general welfare clause (Art. V, Sec. 3) extends authority to powers “necessary, appropriate, or incidental for its efficient and effective governance.” Procurement is necessarily incidental to every government function. Result: YES — implied power.

Does the BOL require national law consistency? Art. VII, Sec. 28 requires the budget to be “consistent with existing laws, rules and regulations of the National Government.” Procurement is closely linked to budget execution. Additionally, RA 12009 (Government Procurement Reform Act) is a national law that applies to all government entities, including GOCCs and LGUs. Result: YES — national law consistency required.

Classification: NATIONAL LAW CONSISTENCY REQUIRED. No Bangsamoro procurement framework has been enacted as of March 2026. RA 12009 (Government Procurement Reform Act) applies directly. The BOL’s budget consistency requirement (Art. VII, Sec. 28) reinforces this. The Comparative Matrix must cover the BOL, RA 12009, and any executive issuances on procurement.

Comparative Matrix (partial)

AspectBOL (RA 11054)BAA (Bangsamoro)RA 12009 (National)
AuthorityArt. V, Sec. 2(f): Budgeting; Art. V, Sec. 3: General welfare; Art. VII, Sec. 28: Budget consistency with national lawsNo Bangsamoro procurement BAA enacted as of March 2026RA 12009 (New Government Procurement Act, 2024) — applies directly to BARMM
ScopeWithin BARMM territorial jurisdiction—All government procurement nationwide
Conflict / GapLegislative gap. No Bangsamoro Procurement Act has been enacted. RA 12009 applies directly. COA audits BARMM procurement against national standards. Parliament could enact a regional framework, but Art. VII, Sec. 28 requires budget consistency with national laws.

Research Answer

Public procurement in BARMM is governed by RA 12009 (Government Procurement Reform Act), as no Bangsamoro procurement framework has been enacted as of March 2026. National law consistency is required — the BOL grants budgeting authority (Art. V, Sec. 2(f)) but Art. VII, Sec. 28 requires budget consistency with national laws, and COA audits procurement using national standards. The researcher must search Tier 2 (BOL fiscal provisions), Tier 5 (RA 12009 and its IRR), and Tier 6 (any OCM or MFBM procurement circulars). This is also a legislative gap — Parliament has the power to enact a regional procurement framework but has not yet done so.

3.7 Common Pitfalls

Pitfall 1: Assuming national law always prevails over BAAs. This is the most common hierarchy error. The BOL enumerates 55 power areas. In those areas where the BOL does not require national law consistency, BAAs govern. National law prevails only where the BOL expressly requires consistency (civil service, budget, elections, audit, IP rights) and in residual national powers. Use the National Law Relationship Test, not assumptions.

Pitfall 2: Assuming BAAs always prevail over national laws. The opposite error. Some researchers, knowing BARMM has enumerated powers, assume BAAs always control. But where national law consistency is required, national law sets the floor. A BAA on civil service that contradicts the national Civil Service Commission’s rules is invalid to the extent of the inconsistency.

Pitfall 3: Citing the wrong BOL article. The BOL has 18 articles with adjacent numbers that cover related subjects. Always verify article citations against the 18-article map in Chapter 5 and Appendix A.

Pitfall 4: Treating the hierarchy as fixed and universal. The hierarchy is not a single ladder that applies the same way to every question. It is a context-dependent structure. The relationship between Tiers 3-5 changes based on the relationship to national law. A researcher who memorizes “Constitution > BOL > National Laws > BAAs” (the Bill Drafting model) will get the wrong answer for areas where no national law consistency is required. A researcher who memorizes “Constitution > BOL > BAA 13 > BAAs > National Laws” (the Strategic Planning model) will get the wrong answer where national law consistency is required. Use the National Law Relationship Test, not a memorized sequence.

Pitfall 5: Forgetting the Shari’ah checkpoint. If your research question involves personal law, property relations between Muslims, Islamic finance, or any matter where Shari’ah court jurisdiction applies, the hierarchy analysis is incomplete without the Shari’ah dimension. Chapter 9 is not optional for these questions.

3.8 Template: National Law Relationship Test

Use this template for every research question. Fill in the three steps, then proceed to the tier-by-tier search (Chapter 2, Step 3).

StepFindingResult
Step 1: Is the subject within the 55 enumerated powers (Art. V, Sec. 2)?[Which power(s)? Direct match or implied through Art. V, Sec. 3?]YES / NO
Step 2: Does the BOL contain conformity language?[Which type? "Shall prevail" (11 provisions), "Shall conform" / minimum standards (7), "Consistent with" (33), Institutional retention (47), "Shall not diminish" (8). Which specific BOL provision(s)?]YES / NO
Step 3: Has Parliament enacted a BAA on this subject?[Which BAA? Check the enacted BAA index]YES / NO / PARTIAL
Classification:[NO NATIONAL LAW CONSISTENCY REQUIRED / NATIONAL LAW CONSISTENCY REQUIRED / RESIDUAL NATIONAL POWER / GAP]
Shari'ah dimension?[YES / NO]
Tiers to search:[List relevant tiers]

3.9 Quality Checklist

Before relying on your hierarchy analysis, confirm:

  • ☐ The research question has been classified using the three-step National Law Relationship Test
  • ☐ The correct enumerated power(s) have been identified (or confirmed absent) from Art. V, Sec. 2
  • ☐ All five types of BOL conformity language have been checked: “shall prevail” (11 provisions), “shall conform” / minimum standards (7), “consistent with” (33), institutional jurisdiction retention (47), “shall not diminish” (8)
  • ☐ The classification result (No national law consistency required / National law consistency required / Residual national power / Gap) is documented
  • ☐ The Shari’ah checkpoint has been completed
  • ☐ All conflict resolution rules have been applied to any identified conflicts
  • ☐ No BOL article numbers have been cited without verification against the verbatim source text
  • ☐ The tiers to search have been determined and documented in the Search Record

Key Takeaways

  1. The hierarchy is context-dependent. There is no single fixed order that applies to every question. Use the National Law Relationship Test to determine the correct order for your specific research question.

  2. Three relationships, three hierarchies. No national law consistency required: BAAs govern. National law consistency required: national law and BAAs both apply. Residual national power: national law governs exclusively.

  3. The 55 enumerated powers are the gateway. Everything begins with Article V, Section 2. If the subject is not there (or necessarily implied from there), the Bangsamoro Parliament has no authority.

  4. National law consistency is required only where the BOL says so — but it says so in 126 provisions. The areas where the BOL constrains Bangsamoro legislation fall into five types of conformity language: “shall prevail” (11), “shall conform” / minimum standards (7), “consistent with” (33), institutional retention (47), and “shall not diminish” (8). They are scattered across all 18 BOL articles. The researcher must check for conformity language in the specific BOL article governing the subject — not rely on a memorized short list.

  5. BAA 13 is the government’s operating manual. It deserves its own tier because every institutional question starts there — who has the mandate, what are the functions, how is the government organized.

  6. Always check the Shari’ah dimension. It is not a separate tier but a parallel system that intersects all seven tiers.
